Topic: Surgery
Question: Obstructive sleep apnoea caused by the following
Choices:
  A: Mandibular ameloblasma
  B: Dentigerous cyst
  C: Orbital fracture
  D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  A: Mandibular ameloblastoma is a benign tumor that affects the jaw, but it does not cause obstructive sleep apnoea.
  B: Dentigerous cyst is a type of cyst that forms around an unerupted tooth, but it does not cause obstructive sleep apnoea.
  C: Orbital fracture is a type of facial fracture that affects the bones around the eye, but it does not cause obstructive sleep apnoea.
  D: Bilateral TMJ ankylosis can cause a restriction in the movement of the jaw, which can affect breathing and lead to obstructive sleep apnoea. 
Action: Answer("D")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  Obstructive sleep apnea (OSA) is a sleep disorder that involves cessation or significant decrease in airflow in the presence of breathing effort. It is caused by the upper airway being blocked. 
  A: Mandibular ameloblastoma is a type of benign tumor of the jaw, which may cause swelling or pain in the affected area, but it is not a known cause of obstructive sleep apnea.
  B: Dentigerous cyst is a type of cyst that forms around an impacted tooth, causing swelling or pain in the affected area, but it is not a known cause of obstructive sleep apnea.
  C: Orbital fracture is a broken bone around the eye socket, which may cause double vision or swelling in the affected area, but it is not a known cause of obstructive sleep apnea.
  D: Bilateral temporomandibular joint (TMJ) ankylosis, which is a condition where the jaw joint is fused or locked, may cause difficulty in opening the mouth wide or chewing, and it is a known cause of obstructive sleep apnea.
Action: Answer("D")

Topic: Medicine
Question: A 60 years old patient who had myocardial infarction 2 weeks back, the lipid profile is done for a patient and reveals HDL 32 mgldL, LDL 126 mg/dl, TG 276 mgl/dL. Which of the following is preferred for this patient ?
Choices:
  A: Rosuvastatin + Fenofibrate
  B: Fenofibrate alone
  C: Rosuvastatin 10 mg
  D: Atorvastatin 80 mg
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Myocardial infarction (MI) is a serious heart condition in which there is a blockage of blood flow to the heart muscle.
  Lipid profile is a blood test that measures the amount of cholesterol and fats in the blood.
  HDL (High-density lipoprotein) is known as "good" cholesterol, as it helps flush out excess cholesterol from the body.
  LDL (Low-density lipoprotein) is known as "bad" cholesterol, as it can build up in the walls of the arteries and cause blockages.
  TG (Triglycerides) are a type of fat found in the blood that can also contribute to the development of blockages.
  Statins are a class of drugs commonly used to lower cholesterol levels and reduce the risk of heart disease.
  Fenofibrate is a medication that can help lower triglyceride levels.
  
Analysis:
  The patient has a history of MI and an abnormal lipid profile, with low HDL, high LDL, and high TG levels. The preferred treatment for this patient would be a medication that can lower LDL levels and possibly also lower triglyceride levels, without significantly reducing HDL levels. Rosuvastatin and Atorvastatin are both effective statins for lowering LDL levels, but Atorvastatin 80 mg is a high dose and may not be necessary or appropriate for this patient. Fenofibrate is effective for lowering triglyceride levels, but it may not be the best choice on its own for this patient with high LDL levels. Rosuvastatin + Fenofibrate may be a good combination therapy to address both high LDL and high TG levels, but it may also increase the risk of side effects.

Action: Answer("C") 
Therefore, the preferred medication for this patient would be Rosuvastatin 10 mg, which is effective for lowering LDL levels and has a lower risk of side effects compared to combination therapy with fenofibrate.
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Myocardial infarction (MI) is a serious medical emergency that occurs when there is a prolonged lack of oxygen supply to the heart muscle. 
  Lipid profile is a blood test that measures the amount of cholesterol and triglycerides in the blood.
  HDL (high-density lipoprotein) is known as good cholesterol.
  LDL (low-density lipoprotein) is known as bad cholesterol.
  TG (triglycerides) are a type of fat found in the blood.
  Statins are a class of drugs used to lower cholesterol levels in the blood. 
  Fenofibrate is a fibric acid derivative that is used to lower triglycerides and raise good cholesterol (HDL) levels. 

Analysis:
  The patient had a recent myocardial infarction, and based on the lipid profile result, the patient has high triglycerides (TG) and low good cholesterol (HDL). The goal of treatment is to bring down the TG and raise the HDL levels.
  Choice A: Rosuvastatin + Fenofibrate - This combination is effective in lowering LDL cholesterol, TG, and raising HDL cholesterol levels. This is a good option for the patient.
  Choice B: Fenofibrate alone - Fenofibrate alone is useful in treating hypertriglyceridemia, but it may not be effective in raising HDL levels. Hence this is not preferred in this case.
  Choice C: Rosuvastatin 10 mg - Rosuvastatin is a statin that is effective in lowering LDL cholesterol levels. But it may not improve TG levels and HDL levels. Hence this is not the preferred option.
  Choice D: Atorvastatin 80 mg - Atorvastatin is a statin that is effective in lowering LDL cholesterol levels, but it may not have a significant effect on TG levels and HDL levels. Hence this is not the preferred option.

Action: Answer("A") - Rosuvastatin + Fenofibrate.

Topic: Anatomy
Question: Which of the following structure is not present on floor of third ventricle?
Choices:
  A: Optic stalk
  B: Third nerve
  C: Infundibulum
  D: Mammillary body
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  The third ventricle is a narrow cleft between the two thalami, and its floor is formed by the hypothalamus. 
  A: The optic stalk is a structure that connects the optic cup, which will form the retina, to the diencephalon. It is located on the floor of the third ventricle.
  B: The third nerve, also known as oculomotor nerve, is a cranial nerve that controls several eye muscles. It runs along the lateral wall of the third ventricle.
  C: The infundibulum is a stalk-like structure that connects the hypothalamus to the pituitary gland. It is located on the floor of the third ventricle, near the mammillary bodies.
  D: The mammillary bodies are a pair of small round structures located on the underside of the brain. They are attached to the posterior end of the hypothalamus and are located posterior to the infundibulum.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  The floor of the third ventricle is formed by the hypothalamus, while the roof is formed by the tela choroidea and the corpus callosum. 
  A: The optic stalk is present on the floor of the third ventricle.
  B: The third nerve is present on the floor of the third ventricle.
  C: The infundibulum is present on the floor of the third ventricle.
  D: The mammillary body is present at the posterior end of the floor of the third ventricle.
Action: Answer("D")

  B: The third nerve, also known as oculomotor nerve, is the third of twelve cranial nerves and is present on the floor of the third ventricle.
  C: Infundibulum, also called pituitary stalk, is a conical process of the brain that extends from the hypothalamus to the pituitary gland and is present on the floor of the third ventricle.
  D: Mammillary body is a round protrusion on the undersurface of the brain that is part of the limbic system and is located posterior to the infundibulum, but not present on the floor of the third ventricle.

Topic: Dental
Question: Pulpectomy and pulp capping are more successful in
primary teeth because of:
Choices:
  A: Increased odontoblastic activity in the young
  B: Increased blood supply through the wide apex
  C: Increased volume of pulp in primary teeth
  D: Lesser amount of collagen fibres in young
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Pulpectomy is a dental procedure in which the pulp tissue from inside the tooth is removed while preserving the tooth's root. This is usually done to prevent further damage to the tooth and to avoid extraction.
  Pulp capping is a dental procedure in which a material is placed directly over the exposed pulp tissue in the tooth in order to preserve the vitality of the pulp and promote healing.
  Primary teeth, also known as baby teeth, are the first set of teeth that come in for children.
  A: Odontoblasts are cells that are responsible for producing the dentin that makes up the majority of the tooth structure. Increased odontoblastic activity could potentially help with tooth repair, but it is not necessarily the reason why pulpectomy and pulp capping are more successful in primary teeth.
  B: Blood supply is important for tooth health, but increased blood supply through the wide apex is not the reason why pulpectomy and pulp capping are more successful in primary teeth.
  C: The volume of pulp in primary teeth is not necessarily larger than the volume of pulp in permanent teeth. In fact, the ratio of pulp volume to tooth volume is higher in permanent teeth.
  D: Collagen fibers are a major component of the periodontal ligament, which helps to anchor the tooth to the surrounding bone. The amount of collagen fibers is not necessarily relevant to the success of pulpectomy and pulp capping.

  Primary teeth are the first set of teeth that erupt in the oral cavity and are eventually replaced by permanent teeth.
  A: Odontoblasts are cells that form new dentin. They are more active in young teeth and can help in the formation of a dentin bridge after a pulp capping procedure.

- Holding cusps are not a recognized type of cusp in dentistry.

The cusps that make contact with the opposing teeth during chewing or grinding of food are known as working cusps and are also referred to as guiding cusps. So the correct answer is A: Guiding cusps.

Topic: Dental
Question: A lateral sliding flap done on a tooth with roots denuded for 6 years will show
Choices:
  A: PDL fibres attached to cementum
  B: PDL fibres attached to dentin
  C: Epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface
  D: Co adaptation to the remaining fibres
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  A lateral sliding flap is a surgical procedure used to gain access to the root surface for cleaning and/or grafting.
  The periodontal ligament (PDL) fibres attach the cementum covering the root of a tooth to the alveolar bone.
  The cementum covering the root of the tooth can become denuded (lost) due to periodontal disease or other causes.
  
Option A: PDL fibres should be attached to cementum, assuming that the cementum has not been lost due to periodontal disease.
Option B: PDL fibres are not normally attached to dentin.
Option C: Epithelium adjacent to previously denuded root surface is a normal finding, especially if a significant amount of time has passed since the root denudation.
Option D: Co adaptation to the remaining fibres is a vague answer that is not helpful in this context.

Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  A lateral sliding flap is a periodontal surgery that allows access to the root surface of a tooth.
  The periodontal ligament (PDL) is a connective tissue that connects the tooth to the alveolar bone of the jaw.
  PDL fibres are normally attached to cementum, which covers the root of the tooth.
  When roots of the tooth become denuded, it means that the cementum has been lost, and the root surface is exposed.
  Epithelium is a type of tissue that covers the body surface and lines internal organs.
  
Answer: ("C") 
The lateral sliding flap done on a tooth with roots denuded for six years will show epithelium adjacent to the previously denuded root surface. The removal of the cementum from the roots of the tooth will allow epithelium to grow and attach to the root surface, instead of PDL fibres.
Response 2:
Knowledge: 
  A lateral sliding flap is a surgical procedure used to access the root of a tooth.
  The periodontal ligament (PDL) is a specialized connective tissue that attaches the tooth to the bone.
  Root denudation occurs when the PDL and cementum are lost, exposing the underlying dentin.
  A denuded root surface is usually covered by new tissue, such as epithelium or connective tissue.
 
The correct answer is likely to involve the expected outcome of the procedure described.
Action: Answer("C")  
Based on the information provided, option C is the most likely answer. When the root of a tooth is denuded, the exposed surface is typically covered by new tissue, such as epithelium. Therefore, a lateral sliding flap done on a tooth with roots denuded for 6 years would likely show epithelium adjacent to the previously denuded root surface.

Topic: Ophthalmology
Question: Cells most commonly affected in glaucomatous optic atrophy?
Choices:
  A: Amacrine cells
  B: Bipolar cells
  C: Ganglion cells
  D: Rods and cones
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
Glaucomatous optic atrophy is caused by damage to the optic nerve, which carries visual information from the eye to the brain. The cells most commonly affected in glaucomatous optic atrophy are retinal ganglion cells, which are located in the innermost layer of the retina.
A: Amacrine cells are interneurons in the retina that modulate the activity of other retinal cells. They are not primarily affected in glaucomatous optic atrophy.
B: Bipolar cells are retinal cells that receive signals from photoreceptor cells and transmit them to ganglion cells. They are not primarily affected in glaucomatous optic atrophy.
C: Ganglion cells are the primary cells affected in glaucomatous optic atrophy.
D: Rods and cones are photoreceptor cells in the retina that are responsible for detecting light and transmitting visual information to other retinal cells. They are not primarily affected in glaucomatous optic atrophy.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  Glaucomatous optic atrophy is a type of optic nerve damage that is typically associated with glaucoma, a group of eye diseases that can cause vision loss and blindness.
  A: Amacrine cells are interneurons in the retina, but they are not the cells most commonly affected in glaucomatous optic atrophy.
  B: Bipolar cells are retinal cells that synapse with rods and cones and then relay visual information to ganglion cells. However, they are not the cells most commonly affected in glaucomatous optic atrophy.
  C: Ganglion cells are the cells most commonly affected in glaucomatous optic atrophy. These cells are the output cells of the retina that send visual information to the brain via the optic nerve.
  D: Rods and cones are photoreceptor cells in the retina that detect light and color, but they are not the cells most commonly affected in glaucomatous optic atrophy.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:

Question: A primigravida came to the labor room at 40 weeks + 5 days gestation for induction of labor. On per vaginal examination, the cervix is 1 cm dilated and 30% effaced. The veex is at --1 station and the cervix is soft and posterior. What will be the modified bishop score for this lady?

  A: 0
  B: 3
  C: 5
  D: 8
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Bishop score is a measure of the cervical readiness for induction of labor. It is a sum of points assigned to five components:
  1. Dilatation
  2. Effacement
  3. Station
  4. Consistency
  5. Position
  The maximum score is 13.  A score of 8 or more indicates that the cervix is favorable for induction.

Given that:
  The cervix is 1 cm dilated, 30% effaced, posterior, and soft. The vertex is at -1 station.

Calculation:
  Bishop score = 1+1+0+2+1 = 5

Topic: Dental
Question: Occurrence of malocclusion in given population is best described as:
Choices:
  A: Prevalence rate
  B: Incidence rate
  C: Morbidity
  D: Probability
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  Malocclusion is a misalignment or incorrect relation between the teeth of the two dental arches.
  A: Prevalence rate refers to the proportion of individuals in a population who have a particular disease or condition at a specific point in time.
  B: Incidence rate refers to the number of new cases of a disease or condition that occur in a population during a specified period of time.
  C: Morbidity refers to the prevalence of a particular disease or condition within a population.
  D: Probability refers to the likelihood of a particular event occurring. 
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  Malocclusion is a dental condition characterized by misalignment of teeth and jaws.
  A: Prevalence rate refers to the proportion of individuals in a population with a specific condition at a given point in time.
  B: Incidence rate refers to the rate of occurrence of new cases of a specific condition in a population over a period of time.
  C: Morbidity refers to the prevalence of a specific condition in a population, as well as the impact of the condition on the affected individuals.
  D: Probability refers to the likelihood of an event occurring, based on statistical analysis.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 2:
Knowledge:
  A: Prevalence rate is the proportion of individuals in a population who have the disease at a specific point in time. It includes both old and new cases.
  B: Incidence rate is the number of new cases of the disease in the population at risk during a specified time period.
  C: Morbidity refers to the proportion of individuals affected by the disease in the population.

  C: Transferrin

  Hepcidin is a peptide hormone that regulates iron metabolism by binding to ferroportin and causing its internalization and degradation, leading to a decrease in iron absorption.

Question: Multi constricted apical constriction is seen in which type of Dummer’s classification
Choices:
  A: Type 1
  B: Type 2
  C: Type 3
  D: Type 4
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  Dummer's classification is used for the classification of root canal configurations, which is based on the anatomy of the pulp chamber and root canal system.
  Multi constricted apical constriction means that apical constriction is present in more than one canal.
  A: In type 1, there is only one canal present from the pulp chamber to the apex.
  B: In type 2, there are two separate canals that join short of the apex to form a single canal.
  C: In type 3, there are two different canals that exit the root separately, but they are not connected by a canal orifice.
  D: In type 4, there are multiple separate canals from the pulp chamber to the apex.

  A: Dummer's type 1 classification is used for teeth that have a single canal that continues uninterrupted throughout the length of the root.
  B: Dummer's type 2 classification is used for teeth that have two canals that join together before exiting the root.
  C: Dummer's type 3 classification is used for teeth that have two canals that exit the root separately.
  D: Dummer's type 4 classification is used for teeth that have more than two canals.

  D: Type 4 root canal morphology is when there are two separate canals exiting the root.

Question: Looseness seen in a recently delivered RPD is due to:
Choices:
  A: Defective occlusal balancing
  B: Passive clasp on abutment
  C: Thin flange
  D: Insufficient overlap on posterior teeth
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  A: Occlusal balancing is a procedure done to adjust the contact points of teeth to improve the distribution of forces on the teeth and prevent trauma to supporting structures. It is unlikely to cause looseness of RPD.
  B: Passive clasp on abutment means the clasp does not engage the retentive undercuts of the abutment tooth. Passive clasp can lead to the dislodgement of the RPD due to inadequate retention.
  C: Thin flange can cause looseness of the RPD because it lacks sufficient rigidity to resist displacement forces.
  D: Insufficient overlap on posterior teeth can cause the RPD to be displaced during function.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  RPD stands for Removable Partial Denture.
  A: Occlusal balancing refers to the adjustment of opposing teeth to make sure that they contact evenly when the patient bites down.
  B: Passive clasp refers to a clasp that does not actively put pressure on the abutment tooth and relies on retention to hold the RPD in place.
  C: Flange is the part of the RPD that extends into the vestibule of the oral cavity and helps to stabilize it.
  D: Overlap refers to the horizontal extension of a tooth beyond the adjacent tooth in a dental arch.

Question: In 4-years-old patient S-ECC is present with recurrent gingival swelling and pain in 61 and 62; what will be your   line of treatment:
Choices:
  A: Endodontic treatment
  B: Restoration
  C: Extraction
  D: Fluoride application
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  S-ECC stands for Severe Early Childhood Caries.
  In this case, the patient is only 4 years old and has recurrent gingival swelling and pain in teeth 61 and 62.
  A: Endodontic treatment involves removing the infected pulp inside the tooth and is not necessary in this case.
  B: Restoration involves repairing the decayed or damaged teeth, which is likely to be the best treatment option in this case.
  C: Extraction is removing the tooth entirely, which is not the first choice of treatment for a 4-year-old patient with caries in primary teeth.
  D: Fluoride application can help to prevent caries but is not the best treatment option for an active caries lesion.
Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge:
  S-ECC stands for Severe Early Childhood Caries.
  Since the patient is 4 years old, primary teeth are present.
  Gingival swelling and pain in teeth 61 and 62 indicate that the caries have affected the pulp.
  Treatment depends on the severity of the disease.
  A: Endodontic treatment is not indicated for primary teeth affected by S-ECC as primary teeth have a greater potential for remineralization and repair compared to permanent teeth.
  B: Restoration could be an option, but it may not be feasible in a 4-year-old patient with S-ECC, especially if the caries has affected the pulp.
  C: Extraction is considered if the tooth is unrestorable or if the caries has severely affected the pulp. Extraction can be traumatic and may have a negative impact on the child's oral health.
  D: Fluoride application is used to prevent caries and to arrest early lesions, but it may not be effective in a patient with S-ECC.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Knowledge: 
  S-ECC stands for Severe Early Childhood Caries, which is a condition where children under the age of six develop multiple cavities in their teeth.
  Recurrent gingival swelling and pain in teeth 61 and 62 suggest that the caries has progressed to the point where the nerves of the teeth are affected, which is called pulp involvement.
  A: Endodontic treatment involves removing the infected pulp from the tooth and filling it with a material that seals the tooth.

Question: A neonate presents with jaundice and clay coloured stools. Liver biopsy shows giant cells diagnosis is –
Choices:
  A: Neonatal hepatitis with physiological jaundice
  B: Neonatal hepatitis with extrahepatic biliary atresia
  C: Physiological jaundice
  D: Physiological jaundice with extrahepatic biliary atresia
Response 0:
Knowledge: 
  - Jaundice and clay-colored stools are symptoms of liver disease.
  - Neonatal hepatitis is a liver inflammation that occurs in the first month of life.
  - Physiological jaundice is a normal process that happens in newborns.
  - Extrahepatic biliary atresia is a blockage in the tubes that carry bile from the liver to the small intestine, which can cause jaundice and clay-colored stools.
  - Giant cells are a type of cells that are formed in response to viral infections and inflammation.
 
Analysis:
  - The neonate is presenting with jaundice and clay-coloured stools, which are not normal, and usually indicate liver disease.
  - The liver biopsy shows giant cells, which suggest the presence of viral infections and inflammation.
  - Option A and C suggest the presence of physiological jaundice, which is not related to liver disease.
  - Option D suggests the presence of physiological jaundice with extrahepatic biliary atresia, but the liver biopsy findings do not support this diagnosis.
  - Option B suggests the presence of neonatal hepatitis with extrahepatic biliary atresia, which is consistent with the liver biopsy findings and the clinical presentation.

Action: Answer("B")
Response 1:
Knowledge: 
  Neonatal hepatitis is a condition characterized by inflammation of the liver that occurs within the first month of life.
  Extrahepatic biliary atresia is a condition that occurs when the bile ducts outside the liver are blocked or absent.

  Clay-colored stools occur when the stool appears pale or grey in color and indicates a lack of bile.
  Giant cells are a type of cell that forms in response to viral infections and autoimmune diseases.

D: Physiological jaundice with extrahepatic biliary atresia - This option is not likely as physiological jaundice is a normal variant that usually resolves within several days of birth.

Topic: Social & Preventive Medicine
Question: Which of the following is used for selecting patients with respect to potential factors that will affect the results?
Choices:
  A: Systematic random sampling
  B: Simple random sampling
  C: Stratified random sampling
  D: Cluster sampling
Response 0:
Knowledge:
  A: Systematic random sampling is a type of random sampling where a starting point is selected randomly and then every nth member of the population is selected.
  B: Simple random sampling is a type of random sampling where each member of the population has an equal chance of being selected.
  C: Stratified random sampling is a type of random sampling where the population is divided into strata based on certain characteristics and then a random sample is selected from each stratum.
  D: Cluster sampling is a type of sampling where the population is divided into clusters based on geography or other characteristics, and then a random sample of the clusters is selected.

Answer: C
Response 1:
Knowledge:
- Systematic random sampling involves selecting every nth person from the population. This can be biased if there is a pattern to the selection.
- Simple random sampling involves selecting participants randomly from the population, which helps ensure that the sample is representative of the population.
- Stratified random sampling involves dividing the population into strata and then randomly selecting individuals from each stratum. This helps ensure that the sample is representative of each subgroup in the population.
- Cluster sampling involves dividing the population into clusters (such as neighborhoods or schools) and then randomly selecting clusters to include in the sample. This can be a cost-effective method, but may not be as representative as other sampling methods.
Action: Answer("C")
Response 2:
Knowledge: 
  A: Systematic random sampling is a method of selecting a sample from a population. It involves selecting a starting point at random, and then selecting every nth element in the population.
  B: Simple random sampling is a method of selecting a sample from a population. It involves selecting individuals randomly from the population.
  C: Stratified random sampling is a method of selecting a sample from a population. It involves dividing the population into strata, and then randomly selecting individuals from each stratum.
  D: Cluster sampling is a method of selecting a sample from a population. It involves dividing the population into clusters, and then randomly selecting some clusters to include in the sample. Then, all individuals in the selected clusters are included in the sample.
  
Answer: C
Response 3:
Knowledge:
  A: Systematic random sampling is a type of probability sampling method in which every nth member of a population is selected for inclusion in the study.
  B: Simple random sampling is a type of probability sampling method in which every member of the population has an equal chance of being selected for the study.
  C: Stratified random sampling is a type of probability sampling method in which the population is divided into subgroups (or strata) based on certain characteristics, and then members are randomly selected from each subgroup.
  D: Cluster sampling is a type of probability sampling method in which the population is divided into clusters (or groups), and then a random sample of clusters is selected for inclusion in the study.
  
Action: Answer("C") 
Stratified random sampling is used for selecting patients with respect to potential factors that will affect the results. It ensures that adequate representation is made of each subgroup (stratum) of the population.
Response 4:
Knowledge:
  A: Systematic random sampling involves choosing every n-th individual from the population.
  B: Simple random sampling involves randomly selecting individuals from the population.
  C: Stratified random sampling involves dividing the population into subgroups (strata) based on certain characteristics and then randomly selecting individuals from each subgroup.
  D: Cluster sampling involves dividing the population into clusters (geographic or otherwise) and then randomly selecting clusters to participate in the study. 

Action: Answer("C")  
In stratified random sampling, the population is divided into subgroups (strata) based on certain characteristics, and then individuals are randomly selected from each subgroup. This is useful when potential factors may affect the results, as the strata can be selected to ensure that each group is representative of the population.
Response 5:
Knowledge:
  A: Systematic random sampling is a method of sampling in which every nth element in the population is selected for the sample.
  B: Simple random sampling is a method of sampling in which every member of the population has an equal chance of being selected for the sample.
  C: Stratified random sampling is a method of sampling in which the population is divided into subgroups (or strata) and members are randomly selected from each subgroup in proportion to their representation in the population.
  D: Cluster sampling is a method of sampling in which the population is divided into clusters or groups and a random sample of these clusters is selected for the sample.

Answer: C
Response 6:
Knowledge: 
  A: Systematic random sampling is a method where the sampling is done from a list of population in a systematic way.
  B: Simple random sampling is a method where the sampling is done randomly from the entire population.
